#  [](/thread/217245-the-dragon)The Dragon

Thank you.  
  

THE DRAGON HAS BEEN BORN FROM THESE FORUMS.  
THE DRAGON LIVES.  

  
  
The dragon is not a mindless mechanical automaton. The dragon is alive. Like any creature faithful to its master, the dragon is ready to serve. Like a seeing eye dog, or a thoroughbred horse at the Kentucky Derby, a trained falcon. The dragon takes pride and aims to please.   
  
If treated appropriately, with respect and appreciation, the dragon will perform very nicely. The dragon amasses victory after victory when in the hands of a suitable master. One who is disciplined. Determined. Patient. And confident of ultimate success.   
  

**ARE YOU READY FOR THE DRAGON?  
THE DRAGON IS READY FOR YOU!!!  
**

  
We can start with a description of the anatomy:  
  
The body of the dragon is composed of heiken ashi candles, heiken ashi smoothed, and 3ema calculated from the heiken ashi smoothed.  
  
The landscape surrounding the dragon has a 200 ema and daily woodie pivots.  
  
The monitoring of the internal conditions of the dragon is done by dss stoch and macd with crossing.  
  
The idea is to anticipate the dragon's moves and be able to ride the dragon. There is much to be gained by anticipating the direction the dragon is going and staying for a ride. The dragon can take one for a great ride to riches and wealth. But if the attempting rider boards incorrectly there can be devastation.   
  
The dragon is giving clues and hints and is very happy when the rider is successful. The dragon wants the rider to be successful. In that way a great friendship and partnership develops. Learning to listen to the dragon.....  
  
This is what the dragon looks like.  
  
_We are working on developing an ea for the dragon.  
Will keep the ea download in progress up to date on this page.  
It is in very crude and beginning stages.  
Please do not try to use the dragon ea for live trading it is only in developmental stages.  
_   
  

**  
**

  * [#4](/thread/post/3394494#post3394494 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 11:51pm  Jan 23, 2010 11:40pm | Edited 11:51pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

Heiken ashi is very significant. The ha candle clearly define the direction.   
  
_The idea is to board the dragon when he is about to change direction._  
  
He changes direction a lot but not all of these changes of direction are good for getting on board.  
  
When heiken ashi changes color that is an alert that a good boarding time may be coming.  
  
It is important to note what the general direction the dragon is going in. He meanders a lot.   
  
The best time is when he pauses, retraces a bit, and springs forward again in the original direction.  
  
The landscape is important. The dragon may be paused near a woodie pivot or s or r area for refreshments. He tends to be very sensitive to these. And he is drawn irresistibly to the 200 ema. The affinity there is very strong.  
  
As the dragon moves along the landscape his internal condition can be monitored. What he is contemplating.  
  
dss stoch monitors when he has enough.  
and macd with crossing confirms when he has indeed changed his mind...either temporarily or in a big way...  
  
It takes some practice to get to know the activities of the dragon. But they are knowable. He is very beautiful. Powerful. And able to bestow immense riches. He is not attached to anything. He is indifferent. And only he knows perfectly the market place.   
  
A good friend to have.

  * Jan 23, 2010 11:49pm  Jan 23, 2010 11:49pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

My relationship with the dragon is unique to me. I go for rides on the 1 min time frame.  
I consult higher time frame dragons, since the dragon is a fractal being.  
Let me show you some photo shots of our activities. You know the old photo album....   
  
with comments on trades.  
This was a practice session using a simulator.  
  
#1 macd and dss favored a move down, but I did not wait for ashi candles to go green, as a result I entered too early, had to ride out a small correction, but this is the benefit of always trading with the trend, because the primary trend was down, the trade was good.  
  
#2. same thing,  
evidently what I am thinking is that I am missing a big move, and indeed there may be a big move in the making, but where the entry is makes a huge difference... always wait for the ashi candles.... they are a a first class indicator based on price action.....  
  
#3. took a chance on a counter trend move, in real trading I most likely would not do that, bad habit, that's good way to get my head handed to me on a platter... lucky only.... silly me, I have so many bad habits that just won't seem to die, Pain of realizing a loss in bad trades may be the only way to really kill them... stubbornness that's all...   
  
#4.little early, dss was not fully overbought, but ha candles confirmed and the bounce down from s2...  
  
#5.[http://cdn.forexfactory.com/images/s...im/chicken.gif](http://cdn.forexfactory.com/images/smilies/yim/chicken.gif) got the entry right, but didn't ride the move. All three confirmations were very strong, plus good bounces down from 200 ema and s2, just [http://cdn.forexfactory.com/images/s...im/chicken.gif](http://cdn.forexfactory.com/images/smilies/yim/chicken.gif)  
  
#6. counter trend, but time of day and way oversold conditions said ripe for a retrace. Still it would be better if I didn't jump for those...   
  
After a big move sometimes the correction is not very great. It lapses into a sideways consolidation even though macd and dss look like roller coaster tracks. The dragon does not actually go anywhere. Buying and selling is going on but the dragon is not moving. An end of day fade can bring a few pips but then again the risk is there for me because of my schedule that I will get caught in the trade and have to rollover. Then I have to take rest also and I really don't want to carry a trade overnight. When I log off I want to be entirely out of the mkt until the next day...[http://cdn.forexfactory.com/attachme...1&d=1264237106](http://cdn.forexfactory.com/attachment.php?attachmentid=399396&stc=1&thumb=1&d=1264237106)

Here is what I would look for:  
This is a minor reversal..  
  
(of course this analysis is being performed post mortem but it can give the idea)  
  
1\. ashi candles changing color from olive to green after a significant run..  
_Maybe the dragon is related to the chameleon family , he changes color.._.  
2\. fresh macd cross a good distance from 0 line. Strongly suggests the dragon has changed his mind.  
3.dss stoch suggests he has had enough and is ready for a change...  
4.he has crossed above ashi smoothed which has also changed colors. and 3 ema calculated to ashi smooth is below ashi smoothed and facing upwards...  
5.he is most likely headed for 200 ema, a favorite which also happens to coincide with r1 2 favorites in one place, hard for him to resist.

The dragon is alive. You must first make friends with him. Observe his movements. Get to know his habits.   
To try to get aboard him is not mechanical. He will throw you off... The signals are there. But if you have not made some friendship with him, followed him for a while, made friends so to speak you will not be able to recognize when he is telling you get on board.   
He is not a machine. He is a living being.   
If you do not make friends with a horse and simply try to hop up on him he may buck. Or if you try to board a horse from the wrong side he may buck.   
Just watch the dragon move through his landscape and watch the monitors for his internal state for a while then we can discuss signals in more detail.

  * [#16](/thread/post/3394694#post3394694 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 6:19am  Jan 24, 2010 2:48am | Edited 6:19am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

practice session with notes on trades  
If you can follow my notes on these trades it will help you to understand the dragon's movements.  
Better yet practice trading on the demo or simulator.  
  
A simple exercise:  
Use a simplified template for this exercise. Delete the 2 lower windows, the dss and the macd. Delete the woodie pivots and the 200 ema.  
Look for ashi change of color. Go long when ashi turns green after a significant move down. And go short when ashi turns olive after a significant move up. With a 1 minute dragon look for 3 to 5 pips.   
  
This is what is called buying into weakness and selling into strength.  
  
This in itself is not sufficient for success. But play with it as an exercise. It will help you to become more familiar with how the dragon moves.  
  
The folowing practice session is with the 15 min dragon. Live I trade the 1 minute but the dragon moves too fast on the 1 min setting so I use the 15min. for practice.  
  
#1. I zoomed out (not shown) to identify the predominant trend. It was down.  
The dragon was at the top of a downward channel. He had tested the 200ema 2 times and turned back down each time. Macd suggested he was turning down and dss stoch suggested he'd had enough. He did test the 200 ema a 3rd time but the ride down was good. ha candles were changing color to olive from green and ha smoothed was changing color also. It was a very dramatic move. Waiting until dss says the dragon's move is ending is a good exit sign. But I invariably jump off sooner. As I become more and more familiar with how he moves I will feel more confident about staying on for a longer period of time. For now. Thank you and take the pips...  
#2 not the best entry point. ha candles had just turned green and were now olive again. dss was making a series of lower retracings showing just how strong the downward move was. hopped in then hopped out right away.   
#3 hopped back in as the dragon dropped below s1 heading most likely for s2. again thank you and take the pips..  
#4. waiting for ha candles to change color was not going to happen in this dramatic move dss suggested that was all there was going to be for a retrace and the dragon may be heading for s2.   
  
Was considering entering short again that s2 was a viable destination but  
macd did not confirm any further downside as there was a very big difference in the angle of macd heading up and the dragon's sort of sideways dilly dallying...   
Time of day is very significant. The best moves are when there is a lot of trading action. This was getting toward NY close...

  * Jan 24, 2010 5:19am  Jan 24, 2010 5:19am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

just to illustrate how significant the daily wood pivots are the dragon has been stripped down to bare bones...  
there are 10 points of interest on this 30 min view where the dragon has reacted noticeably to the pivot levels.  
#1 bounced off s3  
#2 tested and tested and finally broke through the main pivot  
#3 reached r1 and reversed  
#4 fell in a dramatic straight shot from r1 to s3  
#5 bounced up to test s2  
#6 fell to s1 and fell thru s2 on the way to s3   
(interesting to note that sometimes an s or r from the previous day still has power the dragon didn't reach s3 until the next day and formed a double bottom there)  
#7 & #8 tested the main pivot  
#9 dropped back to test the main pivot for the next day  
#10 hovered around r1  
  
In the landscape these pivots are very significant, regardless of what else might be going on. They are part of the dragon's world as much as off and on ramps are part of our experience of driving the freeway.

another significant part of the dragon's landscape is the 200 ema  
There are 7 points of interest on this 30 min view.  
(The dragon is not so stripped down as in the woodie pivot study. He's looking more dignified this way).  
#1 distance from 200 ema is very great the dragon will turn back to the 200 ema  
#2 the dragon tests the 200ema 3 times  
#3 bounces high only to test for a 4th time and then a 5th time to finally break through  
#4 distance from 200 ema is very great and the dragon turns back up to test  
#5 test the 200ema and drops back down in a very dramatic move.  
#6 distance from 200 ema is very great and the dragon again turns back up to test the 200 ema  
#7 tests the 200 ema.  
  
The 200ema is like the dragon's shadow. He can never really get away from it.

  * Edited 6:19am  Jan 24, 2010 6:06am | Edited 6:19am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

From and earlier post:  
A simple exercise:  
Use a simplified template for this exercise. Delete the 2 lower windows, the dss and the macd. Delete the woodie pivots and the 200 ema.  
Look for ashi change of color. Go long when ashi turns green after a significant move down. And go short when ashi turns olive after a significant move up. With a 1 minute dragon look for 3 to 5 pips.   
  
This is what is called buying into weakness and selling into strength.  
  
This in itself is not sufficient for success. But play with it as an exercise. It will help you to become more familiar with how the dragon moves.  
  
Adding woodie pivots and the 200 ema to the template the simple exercise from the earlier post can now be done with the added benefit of awareness of the landscape.   
  
If the dragon is approaching a pivot special attention is given to how he behaves there. Is he testing and will he break through?  
How far is he from the 200 ema?   
All the while watching for the ha candles to change color.   
The pivots can be good destinations. The dragon likes to go there.   
He can never get too far from the 200 ema without returning to it at some point.   
  
_**_Practice, practice, practice, more practice...._**_

Exercise #1  
Following the suggested exercise described previously here are some results.  
Please remember that this is not a complete trading system. It is a simplified template. The landscape is not there and also the internal indicators are not there. This just follows the meanderings of the dragon.  
His bodily movement.  
A good practice is to zoom out and try to identify the overriding trend. In the zoom out we can see what looks like a reversal from big uptrend to some downside...  
So we will look for entries based on downtrend... that is where the momentum will be and also if the entry is not right the worst that can happen is being stuck for a ride while the dragon retraces a little... But he is sure to continue down after he is done.  
first is the zoom photo shot (I had to reload the photoshot so the zoom shot is now at the end of the post)  
then the actual trade shots with the settings visible on the simulator.  
setting is 15 min, live trading I would do on the 1m. but the simulator moves too fast to make any realistic practice possible using the 1min on the simulator.  
then the results... not bad...for a practice session..  
remember also we are only looking to see how to become a little familiar with how the dragon moves and to see if we can identify reasonable entries. We are not concerned with exits here. That will come later..  
Have a go at it. Use this exercise over and over and over. So that when we add the other components you will have the basic form down pat. Etch his movements in your brain so that when you lie down to take rest you will see the dragon. Pleasant dreams..  
Practice, practice, practice and more practice..  
#6 and #7 were very short trades trying to capture the little bit of upside in a brief retrace. Not a good idea to do usually when the main trend is down. But it can be done occasionally.   
When just starting out better not to. Part of the lesson is to learn self control and only act on predefined rules. This was border line, since the minor trend had turned upside. __However it can be a very good way to get your head handed to you on a platter.__ Try it a few times and you will see the dangers.

  * [#31](/thread/post/3397449#post3397449 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 6:34pm  Jan 25, 2010 6:23pm | Edited 6:34pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

adding the landscape..  
the pivots and the 200ema..  
This is a very instructive session.  
Please note we are only looking for safe entries, exits will come later.  
Sometimes the best action is not to trade!!!!  
The dragon is best when there is a clear trend. There are different kinds of trading systems. So many... Some are good in range trading. The dragon is best when the trend is very clear.   
For this session after the zoom out it was not all that clear what the trend was. Suggesting a consolidation day may be in store.   
Trying to trade consolidation day with a trend system is exactly like walking into a whirling helicopter blade...  
This session is very good to show a number things.  
#1 This shows the 200ema (thick lime green line) as flat. Dead giveaway there is no trend. The pivot (thick yellow line is just above the 200ema.  
The dragon will tend to hang out there for quite some time. He will bounce between the 2 and sometimes move above a little bit and sometime below a little bit. This situation occurs very frequently. He is resting.  
Getting ready to move away. Until we know which direction he is going to go just don't trade!!!  
_The worst that can happen is you won't make any money, but that is a heck of lot better than losing money..  
#2. _After a candle (turning olive) pullback, ever so slightly, the dragon headed up. that would be a valid entry. considering he is leaving his resting area and has just pulled back briefly. As you can see it was a pretty significant move up and when we add the indicators we will be able to evaluate exits, but this is simply an exercise to find entries, so we jumped out right away...  
#3 He tore right through r1 without even catching his breath and stopped just short of r2. Without the benefit of getting a glimpse of his inner thinking (the indis) we did not enter short.   
#4 But just see how significant the pivots and the 200 ema are. he just can't stay away.

No. no repainting. Once the bar closes that's it..  
the indis are a macd at default settings with a vertical line programed in for the crossing   
and the dss is actually a stochastic just represented by dots rather than seeing the lines cross, the change of color of the dots is the same as the lines crossing. A little easier to read the dots...  
They are very standard indicators..  
This photo shot shows the correlation

  * [#35](/thread/post/3397700#post3397700 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 25, 2010 7:58pm  Jan 25, 2010 7:58pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

The benefit of using the indicators is that it allows us to view the thinking of the dragon..  
After he took a bit of a run up he tired. Felt he'd had enpough for a little while.  
The macd shows this with the cross. especially since the cross appears high above the 0 line...  
macd is funny, sometimes the dragon can just keep going and going, crossing and then recrossing. so without the change of color of the ashi candles and a cooperative dss it is really too risky to trade for a scalp.  
The dss also confirms with the downward red dots...  
this may not be much of a downward move but it is good for a few pips  
it is countertrend, but sometimes they are alright, just not for much of a move usually...

  * [#36](/thread/post/3397712#post3397712 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 8:20pm  Jan 25, 2010 8:01pm | Edited 8:20pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

as we can see, the dragon only briefly paused...  
I would hesitate to enter long until I could see if he was simply putting in a top.  
I could know this by seeing if there was a divergence in the macd developing.  
the dragon going higher but the macd (his inner thoughts) going lower. So he was going higher but he was definitely losing interest in continuing higher for much longer.  
I will be able see this by the behavior of the dss.  
If the dss reaches a high point and the dragon does not really moved much that wouldbe another clue as to what he is thinking...

his actions speak louder..  
so ashi candles must confirm.  
his affinity for the 200ema is also undeniable.

There are a number of other things to consider. We will get to it.  
This weekend I can prepare some posts to explore the use of the macd and dss.

  * [#54](/thread/post/3415701#post3415701 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 30, 2010 5:38pm  Jan 30, 2010 5:38pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

Where to start?  
okay...  
The dragon..   
So far we have practiced following his movements. Tried entering on ashi candle change of color, then we added his landscape the pivot points, s/r, and the fantastic 200 ema... His favorite places to visit.  
Now we can explore what he is thinking..  
Especially the dss.. It is a default stochastic just expressed as dots in place of line crossings.   
Let's start with the dss.  
In the following chart we can see that the dss takes big swings but the dragon doesn't move.   
He is sleeping. The dss is showing his dreaming. Just like when we dream. It seems real but all we are doing is lying in our bed asleep.  
Macd confirms the snooze. macd is flat along 0....  
dss is really the true internal guage of the dragon's mental state. macd is also very very useful but it is based on moving averages. Dss is measuring his appetite or desire for buying or selling. His desire... And he will be motivated to move to satisfy his desires. That is certain... But sometimes he may just desire and desire and desire and not make a move. Like in his dreaming state. Eventually he will move and in a big way... 

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: sleeping.gif
Size: 63 KB](/attachment/image/404924/thumbnail?d=1365611428)](/attachment/image/404924?d=1264840711)

  * [#56](/thread/post/3415708#post3415708 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 30, 2010 5:55pm  Jan 30, 2010 5:55pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

In learning the ways of the dragon there are many little tricks.   
I use at least 2 time frames. Actually I have 3 monitors and keep the 1m, 5m, and 15m for EURUSD on the screen at all times. I toggle to the other time frames as well. All of them on mt4. Monthly as well. Even though I am a scalper.   
On the following photoshot is the 1m and the 15 min. What I am looking for on the dss is agreement. Are the dragon's long range longings the same as his shorter term longings.   
On the 15 min time frame the dss shows he has a strong desire to sell. Within that 15 mins there were 2 occurrences on the 1m time frame where he also had a strong desire to sell.  
Shown by the yellow arrows.  
(The entry in between the 2 obvious selling points was valid also based on change of color of the ashi candles and change of color of dss...  
we are not looking at macd here... just dss...(But if we were we would see the macd crosses on the 1m as well) 

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: 1 5 b.gif
Size: 51 KB](/attachment/image/404927/thumbnail?d=1365611428)](/attachment/image/404927?d=1264841729)   

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#57](/thread/post/3415715#post3415715 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 30, 2010 6:14pm  Jan 30, 2010 6:14pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

Exercise #3  
On live demo put up 2 charts of EURUSD. (Simulator and charts offline are not practical to do this exercise)   
A 1m and 5m. On the 5m identify when dss is clearly making a move below 80 or above 20.   
When the dragon has a strong desire to sell or buy. Then on the 1m find when dss is in agreement there.   
This is just an exercise to become more familiar with coordinating the time frames. Practice entering when they agree. The entry is further supported if ashi candles change color also. Olive for a dive below 80 and green for a shot upward above 20. Look for 3 to 5 pips.   
This is just one dynamic between a few of the components of the dragon's world. There are many. But too much at once will not help.  
__Practice practice and more practice...__  
Try different time frames. See what he is desiring on the 30 min and how that affects the 15... What is he desiring on the 1hr? the monthly?   
By identifying his desires like this we can see how to always trade with the trend, so even if our entry is somehow not quite right we can feel confident that although we may have to ride out a retracement that it is indeed only that a retracement and not that he has changed his mind in any significant way, just a temporary diversion from his real longer term desire. And the dragon gets diverted a lot..   
the following screen shot is a continuation from the previous post. The third yellow arrow shows another entry on the 1m that coincides with the 15m dss.  
See if you can get the idea...

  * [#58](/thread/post/3415718#post3415718 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 30, 2010 6:21pm  Jan 30, 2010 6:21pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

I don't want to go too fast. And introduce too much all at once. But I only have a little time on the weekends to put into the thread.  
So here comes some more..  
On the following screenshot a strong desire to buy was identified on the 15m and the same buy desire was seen on the 1m.   
On the 15 the dss did not fully reach below the 20 and come back up. Often this can be a sign of very strong buying move. On the 15m the dragon is approaching the 200ema. A favorite of his. and on the 1m he has broken above the pivot. All this helps to confirm an entry long with target 200 ema on the 15m.

Thank you for posting. Your chart looks fine.   
It's going to take a while for all the pieces to come together. We have to get to know the dragon. We can not know him in his entirety all at once. Over the course of associating we come to know him. So the more you can watch his movements the better.   
Like a cat watching a fish bowl. With rapt attention.   
.[http://www.fotosearch.com/bthumb/FSD.../x22295597.jpg](http://www.fotosearch.com/bthumb/FSD/FSD431/x22295597.jpg)  
  
To try to address your specific questions...  
**_In some cases the 2 HA indicators are touching and in some cases there is a space between them and they appear to be longer as well. Does that mean anything or is that just the way the indicators are?_**  
Yes I see the spaces. I'm sure it indicates something. I have not tried to analyze this for my own decision making.   
Since this has caught your attention it may be that over a period of time some helpful bit of insight may come to you from the dragon himself.   
He may be revealing to you personally something about himself that you will be the fortunate one to understand in your unique relationship with him.  
This is what is so fantastic about this system, it is based on a fundamentally different approach. The dragon is a living entity and can communicate with us.   
  
_**Also, does it matter that the DSS is going down well before the change in trend/price?  
**_In general when the dss drops down below 80 it means he is done buying for a while. Or he has lost interest in buying. It doesn't always mean he is interested in selling. Just he has lost interest in buying. That is a good observation that the dss has dropped early. Does it mean that it can predict the dragon will go down soon? Possibly. You would need to look for other instances where this was the case. The more you try to work the system the more it will be revealed to you if that is a good sign to rely on or not.   
I have not tried to use that myself I use additional time frames for reference. You have the 5m posted. I would look at the 15 min to see if this was just a brief pause in his buying and if he was still interested in buying on the 15 min. Like in the previous posts where I used two charts. If dss on the 15 min was going up then I would look to enter when the dss on 5m started to go up again. That is simplified but basically the idea I use.  
_The more you look at the charts and try to follow the more it will start to come to you._ The pieces will come together. It will take time and determination. As you do your own research you will get your own insights.  
The more I work with the dragon the more I think he is unlimited.

  * [#64](/thread/post/3416466#post3416466 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 31, 2010 3:12pm  Jan 31, 2010 3:12pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

Let's take a look at the macd.  
If the dss tells us the dragon's state of mind,  
the macd tells us whether or not and to what degree he is acting on his thoughts.  
From a previous post photoshot the chart shows the dragon sleeping, in his mind there is all kinds of selling and buying going on the dss shows us that, but macd says he is not acting on any of it in any significant way. [http://cdn.forexfactory.com/attachme...1&d=1264840711](http://cdn.forexfactory.com/attachment.php?attachmentid=404924&stc=1&thumb=1&d=1264840711)  
By getting a good grasp of the significance of the indicators we can use them effectively.   
That is why I am taking the time and effort to go into the logic and reasons behind what the dss and macd are measuring.   
Then a cross of macd can be understood in the context of the dragon's overall state.   
Without getting a good grasp of the underlying significance it is exactly like trying to learn to read by rote. There is no comprehension...  
Unfortunately this is the standard of education for institutions in the US and most likely for most of the rest of the world. It's quick and easy. But the results are not very great...

  * [#66](/thread/post/3416500#post3416500 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 31, 2010 4:23pm  Jan 31, 2010 4:23pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

we need to be able to learn from our errors.   
__Failures are the pillars of success_ , the saying goes.._  
If we are not too proud to own our mistakes or blind spots we can really learn.  
The following screenshot from a simulator session shows a number of things.  
I will qualify this by saying in live trading I would not just have the one time frame for reference. Precisely for the reason this practice session illustrates. There is far too much guess work for me with only one time frame showing.   
#1,#2,#3: dss is dropping rapidly but the dragon is not selling much and macd is climbing nicely.. So I take it that he is distracted by thinking about selling but he is not actually selling, he still wants to buy. No short entry.  
also no long entry, since there is Not enough confirmation for me, (again with a higher time frame on the screen it would help)  
#4 cross of macd, dss in agreement, olive candles.. good for a short scalp.  
#5 cross of macd, dss in agreement, green candles, because the dragon is drawn very strongly to the 200ema, that is a good target.. I try to close going into the move rather than wait for the crest and jump out as he falls.  
The few seconds that the broker takes to finish the order can get me a few more pips if I close going into the move, _whereas that same delay for the broker if the move is over and is now reversing loses pips_...  
#6 again the same conditions cross of macd, dss in agreement, olive candles. I entered alittle too early here, and had to wait out a retracement.  
Again with the benefit of a higher time frame on the screen I could have avoided that.  
#7 the best trade of the day...(lesson time - another pillar) A mistake.. I saw the dss going up the dragon is thinking about buying, but he was not buying... I did not wait for dss to confirm he had given up considering buying and was ready to sell. The macd did give a selling cross I entered short.. Ahhh, the mind, fickle...He decided he would buy after all and I took a loss giving back a good portion of the day's gains. Again, consulting a higher time frame would have helped avoid this.. I guess I just can't emphasize enough the significance of using a higher time frame before making decisions.  
Something to note on this screen-shot is "the zone". The area between the pivot line (thick yellow horizontal) and the 200 ema (thick lime moving average line). The dragon will tend to take a snooze there. Maybe it's like a shady grove for him.... zzzzzz.

  * [#77](/thread/post/3418992#post3418992 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited Feb 2, 2010 3:21pm  Feb 1, 2010 8:33pm | Edited Feb 2, 2010 3:21pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

I don't usually think of posting during trading hours since I want to focus just on trading.  
I did manage to capture a few screen shots that can be useful to illustrate the kinds of things I look for.  
I did not place any trades since I was not confident of any strong setups. However the screenshots are helpful anyway.   
Patience is absolutely necessary in order to be successful.   
The tendency is to trade just for the sake of trading. Not a good practice... __Rather that is a good way to lose money...__  
#1. Look for momentum. The trading session should be active and lively. Not lethargic and not crazy with whipsaws everywhere. Just active and trending.  
#2. The general direction the dragon is moving should be easily identifiable aside from all the little ups and downs.  
#3. Give special attention around data release times. I wait until the data has come out and consider trading after the dragon has decided how he will react.  
If I cannot figure out what is going on I do not trade. Market conditions change very quickly. In a little while the whole scene will change and I will still have capital to trade with. Even if I do not trade for the whole day. So what! I will wait until I know what is going on. Sometimes it may be that the dragon himself does not know what is going on. So how am I supposed to know if he doesn't know?  
I will post the screen shots in a little while.

[Info on the Borihei-Dragon Scalping System?](/thread/173934-info-on-the-borihei-dragon-scalping-system "Hi, 
 
I am looking for some information on the Borihei-Dragon scalping system that can be viewed on many videos sites. Here's an example....") 15 replies

okay here we go with some cross reference stuff to multiple time frames.  
I'm used to doing this but at first it can be a little confusing.   
That is why getting the basics down first is really important.  
1\. ashi change of colors for entries  
2\. the landscape and how the dragon is affected by it.  
3\. what he is thinking dss, and how he is acting on that thinking macd.  
(there are _lots_ of other little tricks here and there that can help to minimize risk but step by step is best)  
Using multiple time frames is like the old motion pictures, frame by frame of stills to see the overall movement of a character, or like cartooning... a series of drawings that when flipped through in succession gives the sense of changes through time.  
[http://images.animationfactory.com/t..._walking_sm_wm](http://images.animationfactory.com/thw/thw14/AF/animations/animals/cats/cat_walking/4942440.gif?cat_walking_sm_wm)

  * [#84](/thread/post/3422081#post3422081 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 5:37pm  Feb 2, 2010 4:45pm | Edited 5:37pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

Today was one of those days that I would not trade EURUSD. I kind of got the idea it was going to be like that early on. I focus on the one pair only, EURUSD.  
_The reason I would not like to trade on a day like today is I could not ascertain for certain what direction the dragon was going to take overall._  
I make it a point to enter only in the direction the dragon is most interested in for the long run.   
For the last few weeks he has very obviously been heading down. I would only take short positions. (Maybe a long if it was blatantly obvious all over the place that there was a little upside, even so those kinds of trades are much more risky and can be very expensive just not worth it to me, the stress level is way to high also.)  
  
_As a note: I only trade when I am in a the proper frame of mind. Calm, clear headed, well rested.  
If I have a successful trade I do not immediately jump back into the market.   
I consider that maybe I am even done for the day and walk away.   
After a little while I may come back to the screens and see what is going on. If my frame of mind is clear then I may consider looking for another setup...If I am tired I do not trade.   
The tendency is to want to get right back in after closing a trade.   
If it is a loss then the desire is even stronger. This is a spiral down. **Give me my money back.** It is a trap. Nothing good can come from this type of trading.  
If the trade is winner then the same desire to get back in right is there. **More More More**. Nothing good can come from this type of trading either.  
  
_ The following screen shots shows 4 time frames on the screen at once:  
30m,15m,5m,1m.  
I want to find the dragon's main direction: The 30m will show the stronger trend.  
30m : strong uptrend in dss but in overbought area, possible selling soon.  
slight divergence for uspside macd,   
but strong resistance for dragon at pivot (thick yellow horizontal)  
So 30m not giving a clear message.....  
  
_note: about macd and divergence, divergence is when macd is going one directions and the dragon is moving in the other. macd tells us he is losing interest in continuing on and will change direction. A macd divergence is no longer relevant when the macd crosses the 0 line, and in some case reaches the 0 line and rejects crossing it.)__  
  
15m: almost the same picture exactly at the 30m.  
  
5m: downside indicated. But without being able to identify the dragon's overall intentions I would not take a short position. A move down for the dragon could be very shallow and very risky.  
  
1m. the dragon is hanging out in the shady grove (area between the 200 ema and the pivot)  
  
So not much of help there. No trades...  
_

Well if I can not see anything on these time frames let me try to find his direction on higher time frames.  
hourly, 4h, day, week..  
Where is he going?  
On the weekly he is sitting on very strong support, the 200 ema. He hasn't actually touched the 200ema and still about 100 pips away. A lot of times he will retrace a bit before making a final plunge to the 200 ema. He seems to be getting ready to do that.   
Yup one of those days....   
Even though I trade on the 1 min, I want to know as much of the whole picture as I can. I have a very high success rate that way. But today I can't figure things out. There will be other days where it is clear. No guessing.

  * [#86](/thread/post/3422132#post3422132 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 2, 2010 5:07pm  Feb 2, 2010 5:07pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

Throughout the New York session I kept trying to see if there was any definitive move.  
This screen shot is a zoom out of the 1hr. I was looking for trend lines.  
I came up with a possible scenario,   
given the dragon likes to pull back a bit before his final plunge to a 200ema, and the dss and the macd were saying he may be getting ready to that pullback,   
it seemed reasonable that he could pull up to r1 which coincided with a trend line, (that would give dss time to go into overbought and begin to turn down (as the dragon's appetite for buying became exhausted) and macd would be likely to test the 0 line and reject it at the same time.   
Leaving the way for the plunge to the 200ema from the weekly chart (shown here at the magenta horizontal)  
But I was not about to place any trades on this scenario. It was just something I would keep an eye on, looking for a possible short entry on the 1m at his rejection of r1 and the trend line in order to ride his plunge down.   
Waiting waiting waiting. Went to the store...

(Although I am not placing trades in this study, I think it can be helpful to newer traders just to follow my thinking and see what I am looking for. It is all part of trading.   
Not that a trader has to be in the market all the time.   
A good part of the time trading means doing the research for a trade. The trade itself could be 3 mins. for me. _Those 3 mins can be very lucrative._ The research can take hours. It is all part of trading.

  * [#93](/thread/post/3422369#post3422369 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 2, 2010 6:53pm  Feb 2, 2010 6:53pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

There are lots of books out there for traders.  
One book that gave me a read "paradigm shift" was   
**The Profit Magic of Stock Transaction Timing**  
  
by JM Hurst.  
  
It was a very early work and a break through at the time. Like 1920's I believe. Or somewhere around there. JM hurst was not a trader. He was a physicist and he approached the movements of the market like a physicist would. Purely scientific. Matter and energy.   
(Of course now we know there is more to the market than that, he is a creature with a form, a field of activity and desires.....a dragon...)  
JM Hurst's presentation of the movements of what he describes as a physicist "linear movements in curvilinear space" gave me one of those "WOW" moments... His descriptions of this phenomenon opened up the way I view the market ultimately allowing me to meet the creature that lives there.   
Highly recommend the book.   
It may seem a little outdated for some, and maybe esoteric, but I came away with something of value that's hard to describe after reading it. A different sense of spacial relationships and how they interact in the market.

so now it is the 2nd day and still trying to ascertain what the overall direction the dragon is going to take.  
the 4hr   
shows   
macd: divergence with upside bias (not much interest in selling right now but  
that doesn't mean there is a lot of interest in buying, just not much   
interest in selling)  
confusion is that for a macd divergence to play out it usually has to   
either cross the 0 line or approach the zero line and then reject it.  
the dragon seems to be a fairly good ways a way from doing either...  
(to make things even more interesting sometimes macd divergence lies)  
dss entering overbought (dss can stay overbought for a very long time)  
interesting to note dss has rapidly moved into overbought but the   
dragon himself has barely moved at all, not serious about buying?  
Maybe it's limbo again for a while...

  * [#95](/thread/post/3422436#post3422436 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 2, 2010 7:22pm  Feb 2, 2010 7:22pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

For those who are following this thread:   
Is this helping you to see how consulting the higher time frames helps to avoid unnecessary risk?  
Helps to identify when the dragon is moving in a specific direction and what that direction is and when he is just meandering?  
Exercise #4  
Put 4 charts on the screen. 30m,15m,5m,1m.  
Follow the movements of the dragon by identifying the main trend on the 30m.  
use dss and macd. keep special awareness of proximity to pivots and the 200 ema.  
observe the changes in the 15 m, and the 5m as the dragon moves on the 1m.   
Observe how the dss and macd resolve and unwind on the different time frames and how the dragon moves in relationship to these.  
On a demo place trades in the direction of the main trend. See how the condition of the 5m and the 15 min affect the success or failure.   
Tip: When the dss moves dramatically in a certain direction but the dragon doesn't move much at all, it is a clue that he is only thinking about moving in that direction and this could very likely only be a bit of retracing. Consulting dss on the next higher time frame can help confirm this.   
For instance: If dss 1m is going up but the dragon is lethargic  
And dss on 5 min is going down and not yet in oversold  
the dragon is most likely only a little distracted on the 1 min   
and not serious about going very high, he is sure to continue   
down very shortly...   
This dynamic is there between any of the time frames.  
Test this out on demo. Keep an eye for it as you go. It can be very helpful...

Too risky. Too choppy. Some traders may have a method for trading this kind of market. I stay away.   
NFP could be a nonevent.   
From what I am hearing, the present move up is the dragon gobbling up short orders and will likely take him to 1.40 where he will then take out the stops for those orders that are just above 1.40.  
After that it's back down to weekly 200ema and a rest period.   
Who knows after that.   
The 4hr view supports this.  
macd has to resolve before any downside momentum. which means macd has to either cross 0 line to complete the divergence or reach the 0 line and reject it.   
looks like a bear flag......  
timing looks right, turning point for macd and dss near NFP and ISM..  
When the dragon turns for real, the fun will be trading in and out short on the 1 min all the way down. Pretty much risk free even if an entry isn't quite right. Only risk would be having to ride out a very little retracing.  
Well worth waiting for.

Trick:  
toggle through the different time frames on the same chart, marking the 200ema on each by drawing a horizontal line through it.   
These 200 ema levels are significant for the dragon and by seeing them all on 1 chart we can follow his movements.

  * Feb 5, 2010 5:51pm  Feb 5, 2010 5:51pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

Another indicator I like to use, not always (too many indis clutters things), but some of the time is the trix.  
This is a triple moving average indicator so it very closely resembles the macd.  
Trix tracks the movements of the dragon.  
The arrows are there to show areas to pay special attention.  
They are not automatic "buy" and "sell" signals.  
I find especially useful when trix on a time frame higher than the 1m crosses either the green lower line or the red upper line and begins to come back down.   
These are areas where the dragon has over done it one or the other and will not be able to continue. He will have to turn the other way at least for a little while.   
Used in connection with everything else, this information can help to confirm a safe entry.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: 1.gif
Size: 36 KB](/attachment/image/410185/thumbnail?d=1365612375)](/attachment/image/410185?d=1265359897)

  * Feb 11, 2010 5:40pm  Feb 11, 2010 5:40pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar132912_2.gif) Xivali](xivali)

  * | Joined Feb 2010  | Status: Canis Lupus Arctos | [53 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=132912)

Looking at this system i can see you will make pips.  
  
I do have concerns however.  
  
As you earlier insisted, this system is 'Alive' and so is not mechanical like you said.  
  
As this system is not mechanical, when you are trading this with real pounds and pence, you will have issues.  
  
I say this because the lack of a mechanical entry and exit signals means that you are using **your** judgment and **your** emotion.  
I promise you this is very dangerous.  
  
You **Do Not** know what's going to happen in this market, otherwise you would be a multi-billionaire by now.  
  
As this is the case, you cannot use your judgement and "gut instinct" to trade, because there is only a 50% chance of this being right (not good odds to me).  
  
Again, I'm not saying you won't make money with this, I am simply poijnting out a fundamental flaw, which is that you are relying to much on instinct and judgement with this, and I assure you the FX market is "un-judgeable", it will do what ever it wants, regardless of your dragon wanting to soar with the eagles, if the market is going to crash and you listen to your dragon and it wants to fly, your going to get burnt.  
  
By all means trade this my friend, however i really do see this as quite a big flaw.  
  
However, I must say, the concept is pretty cool ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f61c.png?v=15.1)

Precisely.   
Because the dragon is alive the element of unpredictable is there.  
But to simply approach indicators blindly as if he has to obey the rules with no possibility of exception is the very point.  
I do not see this understanding as a flaw. I do not see that we disa gree in essence.  
The dragon concept rather puts the mechanics and the technicals in perspective. As indicators. They indicate such and such is possible only. Not absolute certainty.   
Then I have the opportunity to make a decision. I do not have to trade a set up if I am not happy with it even if all the so called technicals are in line.   
I think that to overlook the living aspect of both the dragon and myself is a flaw....  
I rather see that to trade in a so called emotionless state is not only impossible but is also unnatural and therefore out of touch with reality.  
Rather a balance must be there. Emotions under control. Not that there are no emotions all. That I believe is an impossibility for a living being.   
The dragon moves influenced by emotions, expectations, desires, fear, etc.  
To ignore this dimension I feel is to miss a vital aspect of the playing field. To have one's own emotions in control is the key to success. Not to deny that there are any emotions at all.  
Best wishes,  
Thank you for your comments.   
Am using another indi that I am finding very helpful.  
rsi 3 smoothed.  
It is the exp 3 moving average of rsi 3.  
A cross of 50 is the alert...  
it is an earlier alert than macd or dss.. but in combination can help to make a decision...

only after throwing all those lagging indicators out of the window. then u will start to develop your own indicator. its called "gut feel" and the more u feel it the more accurate it gets.

  * [#117](/thread/post/3461420#post3461420 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 13, 2010 5:24pm  Feb 13, 2010 5:24pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

Interesting discussion.  
Personally I see it as a matter of balance.  
A system is only as good as the trader trading it.  
Like a great auto. Fast, smooth ride, great tires, etc. but the driver has to use a certain amount of discretion. The road conditions, he may feel some fear if it is icy.. maybe he decides not to drive that day.  
That fear is helpful. He can make a better decision if he feels it.   
Trading is like that for me.   
I have full faith in my system, my good friend the dragon. He has succeeded too many times. So many times. The money is rolling in to be quite honest. Beyond what I really thought could be possible, only dreamed of.   
But I may feel some fear even if the signals are there. Something else may be going on. Some uncertaintly in the marketplace. Greece for instance causing whipsaws. So I respect that fear even if the signals are there and I may chose not to place the trade. Or I may exit early even though the indies are all systems go.  
Each trader is unique in how much risk he can tolerate. How much capital he can trade with, what time frame he is most confident of trading. What system he uses.   
But I think the principle of balance between mechanics and listening to the voice inside is valid for any trader to become actually successful.  
And grow his trading business.   
After all trading is a business.

[Enter The Dragon - GBP/JPY](/thread/75037-enter-the-dragon-gbpjpy "After the Feds, BOE, etc bailout yesterday, who thinks the GBP/JPY has maxed out the highs at 207.97 and will now restart the downward...") 2 replies

  * [#125](/thread/post/3464288#post3464288 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 15, 2010 7:01pm  Feb 15, 2010 7:01pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

Here's the kind of set up I like to find.  
I saw this set up but I did not take this trade because China is closed all week and US is a holiday all day.I just don't like to trade on strange days like these. Sometime trading is thin or sporadic. There is no data release.   
I don't usually trade on Fridays. And after 12 noon New York...  
Frankfurt open is good, London is good. US is good, Sometimes Hong Kong or Tokyo opens if my schedule allows.  
  
What I look for is as many time frames to agree as possible.  
I watch the 1min. Macd was crossing and on the 5min macd was crossing at the same time from high above the zero line. All the indies were in agreement.  
I really like to see whent he 15 min also agrees. And if the 30 is tending in the same way then most likely it is top (vice versa for bottoms) and good be good for a nice intermediate reversal.  
  
I keep an eye on the higher time frames also.   
But the 1m, 5m and 15 in agreement is enough to enter for at least a scalp, 10 or more pips.  
  
pivots and 200 ema need to be watched.  
On the 5m the dragon was leaving the 200 ema while on the 1m he was heading back to it.  
  
zooming out (not shown) shows that trading is range bound, so the move would not be a big swooping one, just a little dip.   
  
the 15 (not shown) was not in agreement but rather showed a strong tendency upward.  
  
I might have taken a short entry here for the scalp, but really I like to see the 15m in agreement also....

Jiva I DO see your point of view, and I think that a trading system must be suited to the trader, and the trader must be comfortable with what is giving him entry and exit signals. So it's all down to personal preference.  
  
I think I read a reply on here that said mechanical principles will not make consistent profit?  
  
600 pips in 5 days  
  
329 this week and it's not finished yet, I am confident in saying that mechanical systems ARE profitable =]  
  
Again, I believe it's down to preference.  
  
Last note, Jiva I have just realized, our systems are similar in the "dragon" sense, I do not use as many indicators as you, but they are in fact similar =p  
  
I will post a screen shot+my methodology as to why they are similar, soon =]

setting stop above or below swings on the time frame being trades.  
here it is the 15 m has the main stops and targets  
but the 1 min is looked to for swing entries and exits.

  * [#130](/thread/post/3475329#post3475329 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 18, 2010 4:57pm  Feb 18, 2010 4:57pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar132912_2.gif) Xivali](xivali)

  * | Joined Feb 2010  | Status: Canis Lupus Arctos | [53 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=132912)

Right so here's my system in brief.  
  
I utilize a pair of 50 period simple moving averages of the high & low.  
These then create my channel.  
  
This channel is where I see the similarities in our systems.  
  
I then wait for a candle to **open** _and_**close** below/above the lower/upper channel band.  
  
If a candle opens and closes below the lower band, that is my signal for a short (sell).  
  
If at any point in time the candle closes back within the channel, I exit my position.  
  
  
I use various Fibonacci points where I move my stop loss to/from.  
The only times I exit my position without question is either at the 423 Fib, or the close within the channel.  
  
I'll give you an example of a trade I took:

  * [#133](/thread/post/3479625#post3479625 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 19, 2010 2:18pm  Feb 19, 2010 2:18pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

I found a fatal flaw in my strategy. I was not careful about the exit strategy.  
I was following the dragon to find entries and trading large positions and exiting quickly. Big gains in a few minutes. That was great as long I was right every time. Kind of like "all or nothing". It works a lot of the time but when it doesn't- out of business.   
I knew it was a fatal weak spot but was not forced to do something about it until.... Casey lowered the boom..  
I have come out of the disaster a lot better for it.  
Not only have I dealt with the stop issue, but now also my entries are much better.  
Surrendering to using stops is one of those hurdles that must be dealt with in order to actually be successful in trading.   
Another one of those psychological issues.  
It's celebration time. I have met the enemy and it is me. I have conquered my lower self, the one with the bad habit and stubborn denial, by the strength of the higher self, the one with knowledge and intelligence.  
Failure is the pillar of success, someone famous once said.  
The template has been tweaked.  
By putting both the dss and the macd in the same window some very interesting patterns can be seen in the relationship between them.  
And adding the OSMA (40,50,100) the longer term trending can be seen easily at a glance.  
Great for scalping.   
will discuss stops next.

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

The xpma and the 8 ema have been removed.  
The ashi candles define the trend without their use. That is the added benefit of the ashi candles.  
I keep the 1m which is where I trade, the 5m and the 15m all open at the same time. 3 computers. 2 dinosaurs that basically only keep mtv4 running and my main system. I like to watch all the time frames to get a feel for the general direction things are going in.  
I look for macd divergences. and especially watch dss for oversold and overbought.   
I don't mean to be impersonal in describing the dragon. This just something like anatomy class..

  * [#137](/thread/post/3479817#post3479817 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 19, 2010 3:48pm  Feb 19, 2010 3:48pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar17305_4.gif) okfx](okfx)

  * | Joined Aug 2006  | Status: Trader | [87 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=17305)

Jiva, I have tried adding the Macd lines on the DSS but I don't know if you noticed already, the Macd lines shift vertically when you scroll the chart. After the fact, they look perfect but are actually misleading unless in a separate panel.  
I am using a Stochs 30,9,9 (just the main line) on top of my DSS 10/60 on the 1m chart. Less clutter. I find faster Stochs like 14,3,3 confusing and misleading as well. They are better with higher timeframe charts. This one catches the bigger moves and is great with divergence, both by itself and with DSS.  
On my chart I have 200 EMA(pink), 200 LWMA(purple) with bands 1, 2 and 3, 10LWMA,shift 3(yellow)  
I also discovered a great strength tool called the currecy strength meter that no one should trade without.   
Here is the link : <http://www.currencystrengthmeter.com/>  
Thanks to Henry Liu for making this unbeliavable tool available free.  
I would like to master the use of DSS because I think it is one of the best indicators ever.

will play around a bit with dss settings you suggest.  
About the macd shifting up and down when plotted along with dss. I think there may be a way to even use that. I see it but it doesn't confuse me somehow (probably because I'm already confused ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f615.png?v=15.1)![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/2753.png?v=15.1) so I don't notice the difference...) Yes, fx trading is my career, hobby, passion, etc. It is really an adventure. And I absolutely agree on the confusion part. After trying out >1000 MT4 indicators (I am relatively new to MT4), I have decided to adopt the KISS style. That is why I like the DSS so much. It is plain and simple, no intertwining lines that keep quivering in real time.  
For me, the other real gem is the currency meter. Definitely incorporate it in your trading. Its best help is that it keeps you out of bad countertrend trades.  
I am looking forward to your input on the DSS.

> [Quoting Xivali](/thread/post/3475329#post3475329 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Right so here's my system in brief.  
>    
>  I utilize a pair of 50 period simple moving averages of the high & low.  
>  These then create my channel.  
>    
>  This channel is where I see the similarities in our systems.  
>    
>  I then wait for a candle to **open** _and_**close** below/above the lower/upper channel band.  
>    
>  If a candle opens and closes below the lower band, that is my signal for a short (sell).  
>    
>  If at any point in time the candle closes back within the channel, I exit my position.  
>    
>    
>  I use various Fibonacci points where I move my stop loss to/from.  
>  The...
> 
> Ignored

gonna get a lot of false signals...... how do you differentiate?

> Disliked
> 
> Jiva, I have tried adding the Macd lines on the DSS but I don't know if you noticed already, the Macd lines shift vertically when you scroll the chart. After the fact, they look perfect but are actually misleading unless in a separate panel.  
>  I am using a Stochs 30,9,9 (just the main line) on top of my DSS 10/60 on the 1m chart. Less clutter. I find faster Stochs like 14,3,3 confusing and misleading as well. They are better with higher timeframe charts. This one catches the bigger moves and is great with divergence, both by itself and with DSS.  
>  On...
> 
> Ignored

Re: strengthmeter.. (the link you uploaded doesn't work, googling it works though)  
nice tool for surveying the pairs. I strictly trade the EURUSD so not practical for me.  
dss 10/60 a little too slow for me. I want to try to capture small moves.  
Faster is better for that even on 1m charts.

Simplicity is best...

some simulation practice with the channels..  
I have put a shi channel on the chart also and I like my macd with crossing alert.  
So the template is little crowded. but everything says something, there are no useless decorations...  
for exiting I am noticing that exiting if a close below the low channel occurs will keep me in a trade rather than exiting if there is simply a close within the channel, little more risk there so I will keep an eye out for that... The 2 examples on the screenshot show how I would have been out of the trade and missed some nice upside if I had exited simply on a close within the channel.  
Your original settings, 50 ma simple hi/lo channel is very nice.  
Of course, because of my nature, I had to try a bunch of settings, shiftings, ma types, so on and so on... but the 50 sma seems very good..  
I like to use the woody pivots, s/r for targets. not so much the Fibonacci, although I will slap a Fib on the chart every now and then...   
thanks for sharing this....  
This is like seeing the dragon in xray vision.   
[http://t1.gstatic.com/images?q=tbn:N...emask_xray.jpg](http://t1.gstatic.com/images?q=tbn:Ng7B4flsPn8x_M:http://drysdaleandco.com/store/images/GamaGo_eyemask_xray.jpg)

Am seeing some real potential "channeling" the dragon ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60e.png?v=15.1)  
Pretty potent stuff...  
using the 50 sma low as the trailing stop,   
and the break above 50 sma hi, marked by an open and a close above the 50 sma hi as the entrance for a long...  
keeping an eye out for woody pivots and s/r which tend to be good targets and launching pads.  
kudos to Xivali, the junior member who is trading rings around old timers...  
and so graciously has given his secrets for free.

  * [#154](/thread/post/3483300#post3483300 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 20, 2010 11:59pm  Feb 20, 2010 11:59pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

Have a little time today, so what am I doing? Practicing and researching trading, what else?  
Very impressive results with the channel...  
This technique could be just what I have been looking for...  
Will need to have more confidence in the system so I don't exit too early.  
this will come with practice no doubt. Another way is to open multiple lots and do a series of partial exits on the way to the target.  
Another really good aspect of the channels is that if for one reason or another the trade turns bad, even when first entering the stop will only be at the 50sma which will be relatively nearby... = small loss.   
And because the stop trails the 50sma the amt of possible loss will only decrease as the trade progresses.  
Another plus, guaranteed to always be on the right side of the trade......

  * Feb 21, 2010 12:23am  Feb 21, 2010 12:23am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

I just happened to be still looking at the charts after New York close when the feds did the surprise discount rate hike.  
I usually just shut everything down after New York, Sydney is always slow.   
But there it was. The big move and I just happened to have a short in place that I was getting ready to close out for a small loss, since I didn't want to hold it over to London. I had a limit order in place and it got taken out in a flash. Then the servers jammed (what what else is new?) and I couldn't back to the broker. Ugh..  
Finally the site came back up and the dragon said go for it...  
All said and done I caught the 100 pip move.  
That was just luck being there then. I never keep the system up at that time of day.

  * [#158](/thread/post/3484214#post3484214 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 21, 2010 10:35pm  Feb 21, 2010 10:35pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

more simulator trades.  
  
Again a testing of the stop that follows the 50 sma in this case 50 sma hi, confirms the continuation of the downtrend and also offers an opportunity to put fresh short positions in place.  
And again by following the 50 sma as the stop all the gains possible from the move are captured. I exited early because of s3 and the macd cross.  
s3 on the downside and r3 on the upside are usually about as far as the dragon will go in a day. Maybe he'll push past a bit, but then he tends to come back in if he goes beyond. That is a pretty big move for him. To go from the pivot point to s3 is really extreme.   
  
these practices are catching the USDCAD during some big moves. I will need to find more sedate sessions to see about false signals.

This is what I wanted to find out. False signals.  
Lots of false breakouts. How to tell the difference????  
Can catch a big trend but the consolidations are murder and false breakouts are murder.  
maybe a retest of the 50sma is a better entrance after a consolidation.  
for long, the ashi opens and closes above the 50 hi, but wait for the dragon to comeback to the 50 hi, if he doesn't close below the 50 hi on a retest it's safe to enter long on the next candle that opens and closes above the 50 hi?

  * Feb 23, 2010 1:37am  Feb 23, 2010 1:37am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96047_66.gif) jiva34](jiva34)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Just visiting | [12,891 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96047)

yes. This 50 sma channel is just the thing.  
first live trades . Little skittish. kept hopping in and out.  
But the technique is very good.  
Especially at Frankfurt and London opens.  
Since this is traded on the 15 min I can trade at work.  
Scalping at work was like asking for a nervous breakdown.  
But this only requires checking back every 15 mins or so.  
Set the stop and put a limit at a faraway target like s2 or s3 just in case there is rush caused by surprise news.   
And away we go.  
The pace is different from what I have been trading. 3 min trades..  
so I will have to get used to holding a position maybe all day. This technique will find those longer hold trades.

getting used to the strategy and developing confidence in it.  
Still jittery, when I see some gains I have fear that I will lose the gains (like that has never happened before, right?)   
but the technique is very powerful and how many times now I have seen that by following it the gains are there...  
So again today I jumped in and out when if I had simply stayed with the rules of the technique the gains were there.   
So I got a little maybe 20% of what was available...  
The next trade shows why I have the tendency to jump out when some gains are there.   
So it is the same old story all traders face, factoring in losses, taking them quickly and letting winners run.

I just have to keep at it to gain the confidence in the system.   
Total for the day was 40 pips after a few more good trades and the USDCAD loss. It can be much more.

  * [#177](/thread/post/3493269#post3493269 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 24, 2010 6:26pm  Feb 24, 2010 6:26pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar132912_2.gif) Xivali](xivali)

  * | Joined Feb 2010  | Status: Canis Lupus Arctos | [53 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=132912)

One thing I will add,  
  
when trading my channel system, If you are the trader who wants to capture the majority of the pips within a move then a more refined exit will be necessary - or so I have found.  
  
Rather than taking pips when price closes within channel, we will utilise another method.  
  
Of course, if price breaks 50 channel, and then within a few pips closes, by all means take whatever loss you were given.  
  
But then if it breaks straight away afterwards, take the trade!  
  
However, when riding a trade, I have found Fibonacci targets to be a more effective method for capturing a greater number of pips.  
  
So, what do I do?  
  
Riding a trade, at the 123 Fib or higher, I set my stop two Fibonacci levels down.  
  
So every Fibonacci level that I 'achieve' in the trade (broken above), I move my stop loss in order to maintain a two Fibonacci level distance between price.  
  
This works.  
  
There is nothing wrong with using the channel for all your exits, however I have found that this is far more effective, and nets you a greater deal more pips.  
  
Good Luck =]

  * [#180](/thread/post/3493849#post3493849 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 24, 2010 9:45pm  Feb 24, 2010 9:45pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar132912_2.gif) Xivali](xivali)

  * | Joined Feb 2010  | Status: Canis Lupus Arctos | [53 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=132912)

Right, First thing you need is a handy tool called 'set Fib price'. (Attached)  
  
I take no credit for this, it is just something I have picked up.  
  
This, when installed, will show the price of a Fibonacci level you have pulled.  
  
So, firstly you need to pull your Fibonacci levels for your trade.  
  
Secondly you need to then open up your trade ticket, and modify it. Then type in your stop loss price, hit enter and bam, stop has been changed.  
  
Then when price in a move breaks (opens and closes above) a Fibonacci level, I then move my stop.  
  
Everytime price breaches a Fib level, my stop moves up a level.  
  
This should mean that your stop is always the second Fibonaccci level away from price location.  
  
I am also in debate as to whether or not I should edit the strategy to move my stop just one level away - but only when price is **about** to break a level. 

Attached File(s)

![File Type: ex4](https://assets.faireconomy.media/images/attach/ex4.gif) [Set_Fibo_Price_Default.ex4](/attachment/file/425891?d=1267015200) 3 KB | 203 downloads

Dear dragon,  
Please take me back.  
I have strayed. But now I see how much I am attached to you above all others.  
There is none other like you. Beauty is in the eye of the beholder and you are the most beautiful template I have ever seen. I can't take my eyes off of you. (Literally)  
You have give me so much, I am ever grateful.   
You have been with me during thick and thin. And seen my struggles and triumphs. You are a true friend.   
In silly foolishness I wondered off in search of better friends. They have all let me down.   
Please accept me once again. Speak to me and show me the wonderful things you show me. I am listening. I can hear you. All the other noises do not distract me anymore. For that is all that those other sounds are. Noise. Your sounds tell me what I need to know. In you sound and sight are the same. Seeing you is hearing you.   
Just see you have captured me.   
I can't leave you.

> [Quoting golden1](/thread/post/3512929#post3512929 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hey Jiva, have you tested (compared results) on a 15/1 setup against the 5/1? ie using 15m crosses as the standard and then 1m as the entry on those crosses?  
>    
>  Brian
> 
> Ignored

Hi, how's it going?  
  
_I got a little sidetracked for a while. Actually the train fell of the tracks altogether..  
_

[http://t2.gstatic.com/images?q=tbn:Q...rriages416.jpg](http://t2.gstatic.com/images?q=tbn:Qhs2aMiZbpjTcM:http://newsimg.bbc.co.uk/media/images/44309000/jpg/_44309815_carriages416.jpg)  

I think you get the picture..  

  
But yes I use them all. I trade on the 1m but I flip through them all. The best trades are when the 1m lines up and the 5m is starting to line up and so is the 15m.  
It's rare to get em all to go at once, but that's a great confirmation.  
Usually the 1m starts the move, then the 5m kicks in and then the 1m starts to retrace, but the 15 is starting to follow the others. So when 1m finishes retracing and lines up and the 15 min lines up, that's a pretty good entry... at that point the 5 min is kind of in between.. So yeah, the 1m and the 15m are a great combo.  
  
Using that same line of reasoning by checking the 30m it is possible to see how strong the move is. If the 30 m lines up, well it's a pretty significant move, then look to see is 1h following the others? and so on... when I find a time frame that is obviously going the other way I can understand the strength and duration of the move. Well pretty much anyway....   
  
It's kind of like seeing animated cartooning. flipping through the pictures gives the appearance of movement. Neat stuff...

For me, I have been using a 1 hr 5m setup for quite some time  
and this, well my very similar version I really like on 15m  
and 1, then I have my 1hr charts open for the other setup  
so if the 15 and 1hr agree when the 15 signals, I know  
I can usually do a bit larger trades on those entries  
especially using the 1m as the actual entry ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)  
  
Yes indeed, was glad to see you come back to your  
friendly Dragon. Its so easy to get sidetracked, or  
let one difficult day make you think you need to  
reinvent the wheel as well-lol. A good setup just  
requires us to stick with it and perfect our  
understanding of it.  
  
All the best, will be around of course! Hope you don't  
mind the company...lol  
  
Brian ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)
